<p><b>Ford Motor Company</b> (<a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">NYSE</a>:&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nyse.com/about/listed/quickquote.html?ticker=f">F</a>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> automaker based in <a href="/wiki/Dearborn,_Michigan" title="Dearborn, Michigan">Dearborn, Michigan</a>, a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>. The automaker was founded by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a> and incorporated on June 16, 1903. In addition to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ford_vehicles" title="List of Ford vehicles">Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_(automobile)" title="Lincoln (automobile)">Lincoln</a> brands, Ford also owns a small stake in <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> in Japan and <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a> in the UK. Ford's former UK subsidiaries <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a> were sold to <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> of India in March 2008. In 2010 Ford sold <a href="/wiki/Volvo_cars" title="Volvo cars" class="mw-redirect">Volvo</a> to <a href="/wiki/Geely_Automobile" title="Geely Automobile" class="mw-redirect">Geely Automobile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford discontinued the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(automobile)" title="Mercury (automobile)">Mercury</a> brand after the 2011 model year.</p>

<p>Ford introduced methods for large-scale manufacturing of cars and large-scale management of an industrial workforce using elaborately engineered manufacturing sequences typified by moving <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly lines</a>. <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a>'s methods came to be known around the world as <a href="/wiki/Fordism" title="Fordism">Fordism</a> by 1914.</p>

<p>Ford is the second largest automaker in the U.S. and the fifth-largest in the world based on annual vehicle sales in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> At the end of 2010, Ford was the fifth largest automaker in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford is the eighth-ranked overall American-based company in the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list, based on global revenues in 2009 of $118.3&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, Ford produced 5.532&#160;million automobiles<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> and employed about 213,000 employees at around 90 plants and facilities worldwide. During the <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_crisis_of_2008%E2%80%932010" title="Automotive industry crisis of 2008–2010">automotive crisis</a>, Ford's worldwide unit volume dropped to 4.817&#160;million in 2009. In 2010, Ford earned a net profit of $6.6&#160;billion and reduced its debt from $33.6&#160;billion to $14.5&#160;billion lowering interest payments by $1&#160;billion following its 2009 net profit of $2.7&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2010results_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010results-6"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-annualreport2009_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annualreport2009-7"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Starting in 2007, Ford received more initial quality survey awards from <a href="/wiki/J._D._Power_and_Associates" title="J. D. Power and Associates">J. D. Power and Associates</a> than any other automaker. Five of Ford's vehicles ranked at the top of their categories<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> and fourteen vehicles ranked in the top three.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_governance">Corporate governance</span></h2>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FordGlassHouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/FordGlassHouse.jpg/200px-FordGlassHouse.jpg" width="200" height="152" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FordGlassHouse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

Ford World Headquarters in Dearborn, Michigan, known as the <i>Glass House</i>.</div>

</div>

</div>

<p>Members of the board as of early 2011 are: Richard A. Gephardt, Stephen Butler, Ellen Marram, <a href="/wiki/Kimberly_Casiano" title="Kimberly Casiano">Kimberly Casiano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Mulally" title="Alan Mulally">Alan Mulally</a> (President and CEO), <a href="/wiki/Edsel_Ford_II" title="Edsel Ford II">Edsel Ford II</a>, Homer Neal, William Clay Ford Jr. (Executive Chairman), <a href="/wiki/Jorma_Ollila" title="Jorma Ollila">Jorma Ollila</a>, Irvine Hockaday Jr., <a href="/wiki/John_L._Thornton" title="John L. Thornton">John L. Thornton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_Clay_Ford,_Sr." title="William Clay Ford, Sr.">William Clay Ford, Sr.</a> (Director Emeritus).<sup id="cite_ref-fmci_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fmci-10"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>The main corporate officers are: <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Booth" title="Lewis Booth">Lewis Booth</a> (Executive Vice President, Chairman (<a href="/wiki/Premier_Automotive_Group" title="Premier Automotive Group">PAG</a>) and Ford of Europe), <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fields_(businessman)" title="Mark Fields (businessman)">Mark Fields</a> (Executive Vice President, President of <a href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas" class="mw-redirect">The Americas</a>), <a href="/wiki/Donat_Leclair" title="Donat Leclair">Donat Leclair</a> (Executive Vice President and CFO), Mark A. Schulz (Executive Vice President, President of International Operations), and Michael E. Bannister (Group Vice President; Chairman &amp; CEO Ford Motor Credit).<sup id="cite_ref-fmci_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fmci-10"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Paul Mascarenas (Vice President of Engineering, The Americas Product Development)</p>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Market_developments">Market developments</span></h2>

<p>During the mid to late 1990s, Ford sold large numbers of vehicles, in a booming American economy with soaring stock market and low fuel prices. With the dawn of the new century, legacy healthcare costs, higher fuel prices, and a faltering economy led to falling market shares, declining sales, and sliding profit margins. Most of the corporate profits came from financing consumer automobile loans through <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Credit_Company" title="Ford Motor Credit Company">Ford Motor Credit Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>By 2005, corporate bond rating agencies had downgraded the bonds of both Ford and <a href="/wiki/General_motors" title="General motors" class="mw-redirect">GM</a> to junk status,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> citing high U.S. health care costs for an aging workforce, soaring gasoline prices, eroding market share, and dependence on declining <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUV</a> sales for revenues. Profit margins decreased on large vehicles due to increased "incentives" (in the form of rebates or low interest financing) to offset declining demand.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In the face of demand for higher fuel efficiency and falling sales of minivans, Ford moved to introduce a range of new vehicles, including "<a href="/wiki/Crossover_SUV" title="Crossover SUV" class="mw-redirect">Crossover SUVs</a>" built on <a href="/wiki/Unibody" title="Unibody" class="mw-redirect">unibody</a> car platforms, rather than more <a href="/wiki/Body-on-frame" title="Body-on-frame">body-on-frame</a> chassis. In developing the hybrid electric powertrain technologies for the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Hybrid</a> SUV, Ford licensed similar Toyota hybrid technologies<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> to avoid patent infringements.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford announced that it will team up with electricity supply company <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Edison" title="Southern California Edison">Southern California Edison</a> (SCE) to examine the future of <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> in terms of how home and vehicle energy systems will work with the electrical grid. Under the multi-million-dollar, multi-year project, Ford will convert a demonstration fleet of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Hybrids</a> into plug-in hybrids, and SCE will evaluate how the vehicles might interact with the home and the utility's electrical grid. Some of the vehicles will be evaluated "in typical customer settings", according to Ford.<sup id="cite_ref-akhrum_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akhrum-16"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-edison_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edison-17"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In December 2006, the company raised its borrowing capacity to about $25&#160;billion, placing substantially all corporate assets as collateral to secure the line of credit.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Chairman Bill Ford has stated that "bankruptcy is not an option".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In order to control its skyrocketing labor costs (the most expensive in the world), the company and the <a href="/wiki/United_Auto_Workers" title="United Auto Workers">United Auto Workers</a>, representing approximately 46,000 hourly workers in North America, agreed to a historic contract settlement in November 2007 giving the company a substantial break in terms of its ongoing retiree health care costs and other economic issues. The agreement includes the establishment of a company-funded, independently run <a href="/wiki/Voluntary_Employee_Beneficiary_Association" title="Voluntary Employee Beneficiary Association">Voluntary Employee Beneficiary Association</a> (VEBA) trust to shift the burden of retiree health care from the company's books, thereby improving its balance sheet. This arrangement took effect on January 1, 2010. As a sign of its currently strong cash position, Ford contributed its entire current liability (estimated at approximately US$5.5&#160;Billion as of December 31, 2009) to the VEBA in cash, and also pre-paid US$500&#160;Million of its future liabilities to the fund. The agreement also gives hourly workers the job security they were seeking by having the company commit to substantial investments in most of its factories.</p>

<p>The automaker reported the largest annual loss in company history in 2006 of $12.7&#160;billion,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> and estimated that it would not return to profitability until 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Ford surprised <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a> in the second quarter of 2007 by posting a $750&#160;million profit. Despite the gains, the company finished the year with a $2.7&#160;billion loss, largely attributed to finance restructuring at <a href="/wiki/Volvo_cars" title="Volvo cars" class="mw-redirect">Volvo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>On June 2, 2008, Ford sold its Jaguar and Land Rover operations to <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> for $2.3&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-r_20080602_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r_20080602-23"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In January 2008, Ford launched a website listing the ten <i>Built Ford Tough</i> rules as well as a series of webisodes that parodied the TV show <i><a href="/wiki/COPS_(TV_series)" title="COPS (TV series)">COPS</a></i>.</p>

<p>During November 2008, Ford, together with Chrysler and General Motors, sought financial aid at Congressional hearings in Washington, D.C. in the face of worsening conditions caused by the <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_crisis_of_2008" title="Automotive industry crisis of 2008" class="mw-redirect">automotive industry crisis</a>. The three companies presented action plans for the sustainability of the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The Detroit based automakers were unsuccessful at obtaining assistance through Congressional legislation. GM and Chrysler later received assistance through the Executive Branch from the <a href="/wiki/T.A.R.P." title="T.A.R.P." class="mw-redirect">T.A.R.P.</a> funding provisions.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> On December 19, the cost of <a href="/wiki/Credit_default_swap" title="Credit default swap">credit default swaps</a> to insure the debt of Ford was 68 percent the sum insured for five years in addition to annual payments of 5 percent. That means it costs $6.8&#160;million paid upfront to insure $10&#160;million in debt, in addition to payments of $500,000 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 2009, Ford announced a $14.6&#160;billion loss in the preceding year, making 2008 its worst year in history. Still, the company claimed to have sufficient liquidity to fund its business plans and thus, did not ask for government aid. Through April 2009, Ford's strategy of debt for equity exchanges, erased $9.9 B in liabilities (28% of its total), in order to leverage its cash position.<sup id="cite_ref-Dolan_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dolan-28"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> These actions yielded Ford a $2.7&#160;billion profit in fiscal year 2009, the company's first full-year profit in four years.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id=".22The_Way_Forward.22">"The Way Forward"</span></h3>

<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Way_Forward" title="The Way Forward">The Way Forward</a></div>

<p>In the latter half of 2005, Chairman Bill Ford asked newly appointed Ford Americas Division President <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fields_(businessman)" title="Mark Fields (businessman)">Mark Fields</a> to develop a plan to return the company to profitability. Fields previewed the Plan, dubbed <i>The Way Forward</i>, at the December 7, 2005 board meeting of the company; and it was unveiled to the public on January 23, 2006. "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://media.ford.com/article_display.cfm?article_id=22465">The Way Forward</a>" includes <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://media.ford.com/article_display.cfm?article_id=22464">resizing the company</a> to match current market realities, dropping some unprofitable and inefficient models, consolidating production lines, and shutting fourteen factories and cutting 30,000 jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> These cutbacks are consistent with Ford's roughly 25% decline in U.S. automotive market share since the mid-late 1990s.</p>

<p>In 2010, Ford earned a net profit of $6.6&#160;billion and reduced its debt from $33.6&#160;billion to $14.5&#160;billion lowering interest payments by $1&#160;billion following its 2009 net profit of $2.7&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2010results_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010results-6"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-annualreport2009_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annualreport2009-7"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> In the U.S., the F-Series is the best selling vehicle for 2010. Ford sold 528,349 F-Series trucks during the year, a 27.7% increase over 2009, out of a total sales of 1.9&#160;million vehicles, or every one out of four vehicles Ford sold. Trucks sales accounts for a big slice of Ford's profits, according to USA Today.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford's realignment also includes the sale of its wholly owned subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/The_Hertz_Corporation" title="The Hertz Corporation">Hertz Rent-a-Car</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Private_equity" title="Private equity">private equity</a> group for $15&#160;billion in cash and debt acquisition. The sale was completed on December 22, 2005. A 50–50 joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Mahindra_%26_Mahindra_Limited" title="Mahindra &amp; Mahindra Limited">Mahindra &amp; Mahindra Limited</a> of India, called Mahindra Ford India, Limited (MIFL), ended with Ford buying out Mahindra's remaining stake in the company in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford had previously upped its stake to 72% in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Chairman and Chief Executive Officer Ford also became President of the company in April 2006, with the retirement of <a href="/wiki/Jim_Padilla" title="Jim Padilla">Jim Padilla</a>. Five months later, in September, he stepped down as President and CEO, and naming <a href="/wiki/Alan_Mulally" title="Alan Mulally">Alan Mulally</a> as his successor. Bill Ford continues as Executive Chairman, along with an executive operating committee made up of Mulally, Mark Schulz, <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Booth" title="Lewis Booth">Lewis Booth</a>, Don Leclair, and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fields_(businessman)" title="Mark Fields (businessman)">Mark Fields</a>.</p>

<p>The domain <i>ford.com</i> attracted at least <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://siteanalytics.compete.com/ford.com?metric=uv">11&#160;million visitors</a> annually by 2008 according to a <a href="/wiki/Compete.com" title="Compete.com">Compete.com</a> survey.</p>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Brands">Brands</span></h2>

<p>Ford Motor Company manufactures automobiles under its own name and as <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_(automobile)" title="Lincoln (automobile)">Lincoln</a> in the United States. In 1958, Ford introduced a new brand, the <a href="/wiki/Edsel" title="Edsel">Edsel</a>, but poor sales led to its discontinuation in 1960. In 1985, the <a href="/wiki/Merkur" title="Merkur">Merkur</a> brand was introduced to market Fords from Europe in the United States; it met a similar fate in 1989. The <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(automobile)" title="Mercury (automobile)">Mercury</a> brand was also introduced by Ford in 1939 but poor sales also led to its discontinuation in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Ford has major manufacturing <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ford_factories" title="List of Ford factories">operations</a> in Canada, Mexico, the United Kingdom, Germany, Turkey, Brazil, Argentina, Australia, the People's Republic of China, and several other countries, including South Africa where, following divestment during <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid" class="mw-redirect">apartheid</a>, it once again has a wholly owned subsidiary. Ford also has a cooperative agreement with Russian automaker <a href="/wiki/GAZ" title="GAZ">GAZ</a>.</p>

<p>Ford acquired British sports car maker <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a> in 1989, but sold it on March 12, 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> retaining a small minority stake,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> and bought <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Cars" title="Volvo Cars">Volvo Cars</a> of Sweden in 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> selling it to <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang_Geely_Holding_Group" title="Zhejiang Geely Holding Group">Zhejiang Geely Holding Group</a> in 2010. In November 2008 it reduced its 33.4% <a href="/wiki/Controlling_interest" title="Controlling interest">controlling interest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> of Japan, to a 13.4% non-controlling interest.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> On November 18, 2010, Ford reduced their stake further to just 3%, citing the reduction of ownership would allow greater flexibility to pursue growth in emerging markets. Ford and Mazda remain strategic partners through joint ventures and exchanges of technological information.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> It shares an American joint venture plant in Flat Rock, Michigan called <a href="/wiki/Auto_Alliance" title="Auto Alliance" class="mw-redirect">Auto Alliance</a> with Mazda. It has spun off its parts division under the name <a href="/wiki/Visteon" title="Visteon">Visteon</a>.</p>

<p>Ford sold the United Kingdom-based <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a> companies and brands to <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> of India in March 2008.</p>

<p>Ford's <i>FoMoCo</i> parts division sells aftermarket parts under the <a href="/wiki/Motorcraft" title="Motorcraft">Motorcraft</a> brand name.</p>

<p>Ford's non-manufacturing operations include organizations such as automotive finance operation <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Credit_Company" title="Ford Motor Credit Company">Ford Motor Credit Company</a>. Ford also sponsors numerous events and sports facilities around the US, most notably Ford Center (now <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Energy_Arena" title="Chesapeake Energy Arena">Chesapeake Energy Arena</a>) in downtown <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City" title="Oklahoma City">Oklahoma City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Field" title="Ford Field">Ford Field</a> in downtown <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>.</p>

<p>Overall the Ford Motor Company controls the <a href="/wiki/Ford" title="Ford" class="mw-redirect">Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_(automobile)" title="Lincoln (automobile)">Lincoln</a> car brands.</p>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Global_markets">Global markets</span></h2>

<p>Initially, Ford Motor Company models sold outside the U.S. were essentially versions of those sold on the home market, but later on, models specific to Europe were developed and sold. Attempts to globalize the model line have often failed, with Europe's <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Ford Mondeo</a> selling poorly in the United States as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Contour" title="Ford Contour">Ford Contour</a>, while U.S. models such as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Taurus" title="Ford Taurus">Ford Taurus</a> have fared poorly in Japan and Australia, even when produced in <a href="/wiki/Right_hand_drive" title="Right hand drive" class="mw-redirect">right hand drive</a>. The small European model <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ka" title="Ford Ka">Ka</a>, a hit in its home market, did not catch on in Japan, as it was not available as an automatic. The Mondeo was dropped by <a href="/wiki/Ford_Australia" title="Ford Australia" class="mw-redirect">Ford Australia</a>, because the segment of the market in which it competes had been in steady decline, with buyers preferring the larger local model, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Falcon_(Australia)" title="Ford Falcon (Australia)">Falcon</a>. One recent exception is the European model of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" title="Ford Focus (international)" class="mw-redirect">Focus</a>, which has sold strongly on both sides of the Atlantic.</p>

<p>In the first five months of 2010, auto sales in the U.S. rose to 4.6&#160;million cars and light trucks, an increase of 17% from a year earlier. The rise was mainly caused by the return of commercial customers that had all but stopped buying in 2009 during the recession. Sales to individual customers at dealerships have increased 13%, while fleet sales have jumped 32%.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford reported that 37% of its sales in May came from fleet sales when it announced its sales for the month increased 23%.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> In the first seven months of 2010, vehicle sales of Ford increased 24%, including retail and fleet sales. Fleet sales of Ford for the same period rose 35% to 386,000 units while retail sales increase 19%. Fleet sales account for 39 percent of Chrysler's sales and 31 percent for GM's.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:250px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benfield_Ford,_Wetherby_(April_2010)_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Benfield_Ford%2C_Wetherby_%28April_2010%29_001.jpg/248px-Benfield_Ford%2C_Wetherby_%28April_2010%29_001.jpg" width="248" height="186" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benfield_Ford,_Wetherby_(April_2010)_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

A British Ford dealership in <a href="/wiki/Wetherby" title="Wetherby">Wetherby</a>, West Yorkshire.</div>

</div>

</div>

<p>At first, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Germany" title="Ford Germany">Ford in Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_of_Britain" title="Ford of Britain">Ford in Britain</a> built different models from one another until the late 1960s, with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_(Europe)" title="Ford Escort (Europe)">Ford Escort</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Capri" title="Ford Capri">Ford Capri</a> being common to both companies. Later on, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Taunus" title="Ford Taunus">Ford Taunus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cortina" title="Ford Cortina">Ford Cortina</a> became identical, produced in <a href="/wiki/Left_hand_drive" title="Left hand drive" class="mw-redirect">left hand drive</a> and right hand drive respectively. Rationalisation of model ranges meant that production of many models in the UK switched to elsewhere in Europe, including Belgium and Spain as well as Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Ford Sierra</a> replaced the Taunus and Cortina in 1982, drawing criticism for its radical aerodynamic styling, which was soon given nicknames such as "Jellymould" and "The Salesman's Spaceship."</p>

<p>Increasingly, the Ford Motor Company has looked to <a href="/wiki/Ford_Europe" title="Ford Europe" class="mw-redirect">Ford of Europe</a> for its "world cars", such as the Mondeo, Focus, and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Fiesta</a>, although sales of European-sourced Fords in the U.S. have been disappointing. The Focus has been one exception to this, which has become America's best selling compact car since its launch in 2000.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources from July 2007">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<p>In February 2002, Ford ended car production in the UK. It was the first time in 90 years that Ford cars had not been made in Britain, although production of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit" title="Ford Transit">Transit</a> van continues at the company's <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a> facility, engines at <a href="/wiki/Bridgend" title="Bridgend">Bridgend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Dagenham" title="Ford Dagenham">Dagenham</a>, and transmissions at <a href="/wiki/Halewood" title="Halewood">Halewood</a>. Development of European Ford is broadly split between <a href="/wiki/Dunton_Wayletts" title="Dunton Wayletts">Dunton</a> in Essex (powertrain, Fiesta/Ka, and commercial vehicles) and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> (body, chassis, electrical, Focus, Mondeo) in Germany. Ford also produced the <a href="/wiki/Thames_Trader" title="Thames Trader">Thames</a> range of commercial vehicles, although the use of this brand name was discontinued circa 1965. Elsewhere in continental Europe, Ford assembles the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Mondeo</a> range in <a href="/wiki/Genk" title="Genk">Genk</a> (Belgium), Fiesta in <a href="/wiki/Valencia_(city_in_Spain)" title="Valencia (city in Spain)" class="mw-redirect">Valencia</a> (Spain) and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> (Germany), Ka in Valencia, and Focus in Valencia, <a href="/wiki/Saarlouis" title="Saarlouis">Saarlouis</a> (Germany) and <a href="/wiki/Vsevolozhsk" title="Vsevolozhsk">Vsevolozhsk</a> (Russia). Transit production is in <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmit" title="İzmit">Kocaeli</a> (Turkey), <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a> (UK), and Transit Connect in <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmit" title="İzmit">Kocaeli</a>.</p>

<p>Ford also owns a joint-venture production plant in Turkey. <a href="/wiki/Otosan" title="Otosan">Ford-Otosan</a>, established in the 1970s, manufactures the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Connect" title="Ford Transit Connect">Transit Connect</a> compact panel van as well as the "Jumbo" and long-wheelbase versions of the full-size Transit. This new production facility was set up near <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmit" title="İzmit">Kocaeli</a> in 2002, and its opening marked the end of Transit assembly in Genk.</p>

<p>Another joint venture plant near <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal" title="Setúbal">Setúbal</a> in Portugal, set up in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, formerly assembled the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Galaxy" title="Ford Galaxy">Galaxy</a> people-carrier as well as its sister ships, the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Sharan" title="Volkswagen Sharan">VW Sharan</a> and <a href="/wiki/SEAT_Alhambra" title="SEAT Alhambra">SEAT Alhambra</a>. With the introduction of the third generation of the Galaxy, Ford has moved the production of the people-carrier to the Genk plant, with Volkswagen taking over sole ownership of the Setúbal facility.</p>

<p>In 2008, Ford acquired a majority stake in <a href="/wiki/Automobile_Craiova" title="Automobile Craiova">Automobile Craiova</a>, Romania. Starting 2009, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Connect" title="Ford Transit Connect">Ford Transit Connect</a> will be Ford's first model produced in <a href="/wiki/Craiova" title="Craiova">Craiova</a>, followed, in 2010, by low-capacity car engines and a new small class car.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Ford Europe has broken new ground with a number of relatively futuristic car launches over the last 50 years.</p>

<p>Its 1959 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Anglia" title="Ford Anglia">Anglia</a> two-door saloon was one of the most quirky-looking small family cars in Europe at the time of its launch, but buyers soon became accustomed to its looks and it was hugely popular with British buyers in particular. It was still selling well when replaced by the more practical <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_(Europe)" title="Ford Escort (Europe)">Escort</a> in 1967.</p>

<p>The third incarnation of the Ford Escort was launched in 1980 and marked the company's move from rear-wheel drive saloons to front-wheel drive hatchbacks in the small family car sector.</p>

<p>The fourth generation Escort was produced from 1990 until 2000, although its successor – the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" title="Ford Focus (international)" class="mw-redirect">Focus</a> – had been on sale since 1998. On its launch, the Focus was arguably the most dramatic-looking and fine-handling small family cars on sale, and sold in huge volumes right up to the launch of the next generation Focus at the end of 2004.</p>

<p>The 1982 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Ford Sierra</a> – replacement for the long-running and massively popular <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cortina" title="Ford Cortina">Cortina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Taunus" title="Ford Taunus">Taunus</a> models – was a style-setter at the time of its launch. Its ultramodern aerodynamic design was a world away from a boxy, sharp-edged Cortina, and it was massively popular just about everywhere it was sold. A series of updates kept it looking relatively fresh until it was replaced by the front-wheel drive <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Mondeo</a> at the start of 1993.</p>

<p>The rise in popularity of small cars during the 1970s saw Ford enter the mini-car market in 1976 with its <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Fiesta</a> hatchback. Most of its production was concentrated at <a href="/wiki/Valencia,_Spain" title="Valencia, Spain">Valencia</a> in Spain, and the Fiesta sold in huge figures from the very start. An update in 1983 and the launch of an all-new model in 1989 strengthened its position in the small car market.</p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Asia_Pacific">Asia Pacific</span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:250px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SaigonFord.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fa/SaigonFord.jpg/248px-SaigonFord.jpg" width="248" height="170" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SaigonFord.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

Ford dealership in <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City" title="Ho Chi Minh City">Ho Chi Minh City</a>, Vietnam (August 2005)</div>

</div>

</div>

<p>In Australia and New Zealand, the popular <a href="/wiki/Ford_Falcon_(Australia)" title="Ford Falcon (Australia)">Ford Falcon</a> has long been considered the average family car and is considerably larger than the Mondeo, Ford's largest car sold in Europe. Between 1960 and 1972, the Falcon was based on a U.S. model of the same name, but since then has been entirely designed and manufactured in Australia, occasionlly being manufactured in New Zealand. Like its <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> rival, the <a href="/wiki/Holden_Commodore" title="Holden Commodore">Holden Commodore</a>, the Falcon uses a rear wheel drive layout. High performance variants of the Falcon running locally built engines produce up to 362&#160;hp (270&#160;kW). A <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9_utility" title="Coupé utility">ute</a> (short for "utility", known in the US as <a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">pickup truck</a>) version is also available with the same range of drivetrains. In addition, Ford Australia sells highly tuned limited-production Falcon sedans and <a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">utes</a> through its performance car division, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Performance_Vehicles" title="Ford Performance Vehicles">Ford Performance Vehicles</a>.</p>

<p>In Australia, the Commodore and Falcon have traditionally outsold all other cars and comprise over 20% of the new car market. In New Zealand, Ford was second in market share in the first eight months of 2006 with 14.4 per cent.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> More recently Ford has axed its Falcon-based LWB variant of its lineup – the Fairlane and LTD ranges, and announced that their Geelong engine manufacturing plant may be shut down from 2013. They have also announced local manufacturing of the Focus small car starting from 2011.</p>

<p>However, with the acquisition of a stake in Japanese manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> in 1979, Ford began selling Mazda's Familia and Capella (also known as the <a href="/wiki/Mazda_Familia" title="Mazda Familia">323</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazda_626" title="Mazda 626">626</a>) as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Laser" title="Ford Laser">Ford Laser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Telstar" title="Ford Telstar">Telstar</a>, replacing the European-sourced Escort and Cortina.</p>

<p>In Australia, the Laser was one of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Australia" title="Ford Motor Company of Australia">Ford Australia</a>'s most successful models, and was manufactured in Ford's <a href="/wiki/Homebush,_New_South_Wales" title="Homebush, New South Wales">Homebush</a> plant from 1981 until the plant's closure in September 1994. It outsold the Mazda 323, despite being almost identical to it, due to the fact the Laser was manufactured in Australia and Ford was perceived as a local brand.</p>

<p>In New Zealand, the Ford Laser and Telstar were assembled alongside the Mazda 323 and 626 until 1997, at the Vehicle Assemblers of New Zealand (VANZ) plant in <a href="/wiki/Wiri" title="Wiri">Wiri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Sierra</a> wagon was also assembled in New Zealand, owing to the popularity of <a href="/wiki/Station_wagon" title="Station wagon">station wagons</a> in that market.</p>

<p>Through its relationship with Mazda, Ford also acquired a stake in South Korean manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" title="Kia Motors">Kia</a>, which built the (Mazda-based) <a href="/wiki/Ford_Festiva" title="Ford Festiva">Ford Festiva</a> from 1988–1993, and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Festiva" title="Ford Festiva">Ford Aspire</a> from 1994–1997 for export to the United States, but later sold their interest to <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai</a> (which also manufactured the Ford Cortina until the 1980s). Kia continued to market the Aspire as the Kia Avella, later replaced by the Rio and once again sold in the US.</p>

<p>Ford's presence in Asia has traditionally been much smaller, confined to <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, Singapore, Hong Kong, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, where Ford has had a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Ford_Lio_Ho" title="Ford Lio Ho">Lio Ho</a> since the 1970s. Ford began assembly of cars in Thailand in 1960, but withdrew from the country in 1976, and did not return until 1995, when it formed a joint venture with Mazda called Auto Alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Ford_India_Private_Limited" title="Ford India Private Limited">Ford India</a> began production in 1998 with its Ford Escort model, which was later replaced by locally produced <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ikon" title="Ford Ikon">Ford Ikon</a> in 2001. It has since added Fusion, Fiesta, Mondeo and Endeavour to its product line.</p>

<p>On March 9, 2010, Ford Motor Co. launched its first made-for-India compact car. Starting at 349,900 ($7,690), the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Figo" title="Ford Figo">Figo</a> is Ford's first car designed and priced for the mass Indian market.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>On July 28, 2011 Ford India signs MoU with the State of <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> to build assembly and engine plant in <a href="/wiki/Sanand" title="Sanand">Sanand</a> and will invest approximately US$1 billion on a 460-acre site.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span></h3>

<p>In South America, Ford has had to face protectionist government measures in each country, with the result that it built different models in different countries, without particular regard to rationalization or <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_scale" title="Economy of scale" class="mw-redirect">economy of scale</a> inherent to producing and sharing similar vehicles between the nations. In many cases, new vehicles in a country were based on those of the other manufacturers it had entered into production agreements with, or whose factories it had acquired. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Corcel" title="Ford Corcel">Corcel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Del_Rey" title="Ford Del Rey">Del Rey</a> in Brazil were originally based on <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> vehicles.</p>

<p>In 1987, <a href="/wiki/Ford_do_Brasil" title="Ford do Brasil">Ford of Brasil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Argentina" title="Ford Motor Company of Argentina">Ford of Argentina</a> merged its operations with those of <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> to form a company called <a href="/wiki/Autolatina" title="Autolatina">Autolatina</a>, with which it shared models. Sales figures and profitability were disappointing, and Autolatina was dissolved in 1995. With the advent of <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>, the regional common market, Ford was finally able to rationalize its product line-ups in those countries. Consequently, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Ford Fiesta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_EcoSport" title="Ford EcoSport">Ford EcoSport</a> are only built in Brazil, and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" title="Ford Focus (international)" class="mw-redirect">Ford Focus</a> only built in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, with each plant exporting in large volumes to the neighboring countries. Models like the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Ford Mondeo</a> from Europe could now be imported completely built up. Ford of Brazil produces a pick-up truck version of the Fiesta, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Courier" title="Ford Courier">Courier</a>, which is also produced in South Africa as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Bantam" title="Ford Bantam">Ford Bantam</a> in <a href="/wiki/Driving_on_the_left_or_right" title="Driving on the left or right" class="mw-redirect">right hand drive</a> versions.</p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Africa_and_Middle_East">Africa and Middle East</span></h3>

<p>In Africa, Ford's market presence has traditionally been strongest in South Africa and neighbouring countries, with only trucks being sold elsewhere on the continent. Ford in South Africa began by importing kits from Canada to be assembled at its Port Elizabeth facility. Later Ford sourced its models from the UK and Australia, with local versions of the Ford Cortina including the XR6, with a 3.0 V6 engine, and a <a href="/wiki/Ford_P100" title="Ford P100">Cortina-based 'bakkie' or pick-up</a>, which was exported to the UK. In the mid-1980s Ford merged with a rival company, owned by <a href="/wiki/Anglo_American_plc" title="Anglo American plc">Anglo American</a>, to form the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Motor_Corporation" title="South African Motor Corporation" class="mw-redirect">South African Motor Corporation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Samcor" title="Samcor">Samcor</a>).</p>

<p>Following international condemnation of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid" class="mw-redirect">apartheid</a>, Ford divested from South Africa in 1988, and sold its stake in Samcor, although it licensed the use of its brand name to the company. Samcor began to assemble Mazdas as well, which affected its product line-up, and saw the European Fords like the Escort and Sierra replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a>-based Laser and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Telstar" title="Ford Telstar">Telstar</a>. Ford bought a 45 per cent stake in <a href="/wiki/Samcor" title="Samcor">Samcor</a> following the demise of apartheid in 1994, and this later became, once again, a wholly owned subsidiary, the Ford Motor Company of Southern Africa. Ford now sells a local sedan version of the Fiesta (also built in India and Mexico), and the Focus. The Falcon model from Australia was also sold in South Africa, but was dropped in 2003, while the Mondeo, after briefly being assembled locally, was dropped in 2005.</p>

<p>Ford's market presence in the Middle East has traditionally been even smaller, partly due to previous Arab boycotts of companies dealing with Israel. Ford and Lincoln vehicles are currently marketed in ten countries in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, Kuwait, and the <a href="/wiki/UAE" title="UAE" class="mw-redirect">UAE</a> are the biggest markets. Ford also established itself in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> in 1926, but faced an uphill battle during the 1950s due to the hostile nationalist business environment.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford's distributor in Saudi Arabia announced in February 2003 that it had sold 100,000 Ford and Lincoln vehicles since commencing sales in November 1986. Half of the Ford/Lincoln vehicles sold in that country were <a href="/wiki/Ford_Crown_Victoria" title="Ford Crown Victoria">Ford Crown Victorias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, Ford sold 30,000 units in the region, falling far short of <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Corporation" title="General Motors Corporation" class="mw-redirect">General Motors</a>' 88,852 units and <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Motors" title="Nissan Motors">Nissan Motors</a>' 75,000 units.</p>

<p>Ford announced in late 2008 July that it will bring six of its more fuel-efficient European models to the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Compressed_natural_gas">Compressed natural gas</span></h3>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fossil_fuel" title="Alternative fossil fuel" class="mw-redirect">alternative fossil fuel</a> vehicles, such as some versions of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Victoria" title="Crown Victoria" class="mw-redirect">Crown Victoria</a> especially in fleet and taxi service, operate on <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">compressed natural gas</a>—or CNG. Some CNG vehicles have dual fuel tanks – one for gasoline, the other for CNG – the same engine can operate on either fuel via a selector switch.</p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Flexible_fuel_vehicles">Flexible fuel vehicles</span></h3>

<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Flexible_fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible fuel vehicle" class="mw-redirect">Flexible fuel vehicle</a></div>

<p><a href="/wiki/Flexible_fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible fuel vehicle" class="mw-redirect">Flexible fuel vehicles</a> are designed to operate smoothly using a wide range of available <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol fuel</a> mixtures—from pure gasoline, to <a href="/wiki/Bioethanol" title="Bioethanol" class="mw-redirect">bioethanol</a>-gasoline blends such as <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> (85% <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol</a> and 15% gasoline) or <a href="/wiki/Common_ethanol_fuel_mixtures" title="Common ethanol fuel mixtures">E100</a> (neat <a href="/wiki/Hydrous" title="Hydrous" class="mw-redirect">hydrous</a> ethanol) in Brazil. Part of the challenge of successful marketing alternative and flexible fuel vehicles in the U.S., is the general lack of establishment of sufficient <a href="/wiki/Fueling_station" title="Fueling station" class="mw-redirect">fueling stations</a>, which would be essential for these vehicles to be attractive to a wide range of consumers. Significant efforts to ramp up production and distribution of <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> fuels are underway and expanding.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Ford is also planning to produce 250,000 E85-capable vehicles a year in the US, adding to some 1.6&#160;million already sold in the last 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Current Ford E85 Flexible Fuel Vehicles sold in North America and Europe are:<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<ul>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_F-150" title="Ford F-150" class="mw-redirect">Ford F-150</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Crown_Victoria" title="Ford Crown Victoria">Ford Crown Victoria</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" title="Ford Focus (international)" class="mw-redirect">Ford Focus</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_C-MAX" title="Ford C-MAX" class="mw-redirect">Ford C-MAX</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Ford Mondeo</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_S-MAX" title="Ford S-MAX" class="mw-redirect">Ford S-MAX</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Galaxy" title="Ford Galaxy">Ford Galaxy</a></li>
