<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_vehicles">Electric vehicles</span></h3>

<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">Electric vehicle</a></div>

<p>Ford Motor Co. expects <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a> will represent a "major portion" of its lineup a decade from now as the automaker breaks away from a recent reliance on pickup trucks and SUVs. The stakes are high because Ford's stepped-up investment is coming at a time when the U.S. government is demanding steep increases in fuel economy and has put money forward to help automakers adopt new fuel-saving technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-autoblog_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autoblog-63"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Ford Motor Co. will partner with <a href="/wiki/Coulomb_Technologies" title="Coulomb Technologies">Coulomb Technologies</a> to provide nearly 5,000 free in-home <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">charging stations</a> for some of the automaker's first electric vehicle customers, under the Ford <a href="/w/index.php?title=Blue_Oval_ChargePoint_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Blue Oval ChargePoint Program (page does not exist)">Blue Oval ChargePoint Program</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h4> <span class="mw-headline" id="Hybrid_electric_vehicles">Hybrid electric vehicles</span></h4>

<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">Hybrid electric vehicle</a></div>

<p>In 2004 both Ford and Toyota agreed on a patent sharing accord which granted Ford access to certain hybrid technology patented by Toyota, in exchange Ford licensed Toyota some of their own patents.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Ford did improve <a href="/wiki/Fuel_efficiency" title="Fuel efficiency">fuel efficiency</a> during 2005, with the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Hybrid-Electric Escape</a>. With this vehicle, Ford was third to the automotive market with a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid electric vehicle</a> and the first hybrid electric <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUV</a> to market. This was also the first hybrid electric vehicle with a <a href="/wiki/Flexible_fuel" title="Flexible fuel" class="mw-redirect">flexible fuel</a> capability to run on <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The Escape's platform mate <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Mariner" title="Mercury Mariner">Mercury Mariner</a> was also available with the hybrid-electric system in the 2006 model year—a full year ahead of schedule. The similar <a href="/wiki/Mazda_Tribute" title="Mazda Tribute">Mazda Tribute</a> will also receive a hybrid-electric powertrain option, along with many other vehicles in the Ford vehicle line.</p>

<p>In 2005 Ford announced its goal to make 250,000 hybrids a year by 2010, but by mid-2006 announced that it would not meet that goal, due to excessively high costs and the lack of sufficient supplies of the hybrid-electric batteries and drivetrain system components.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Instead, Ford has committed to accelerating development of next-generation hybrid-electric power plants in Britain, in collaboration with Volvo. This engineering study is expected to yield more than 100 new hybrid-electric vehicle models and derivatives. There are also plans for hybrid versions of the Ford Edge and Lincoln MKX.</p>

<p><a href="/wiki/Ford" title="Ford" class="mw-redirect">Ford</a> announced on 2007-07-09 that it will team up with <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Edison" title="Southern California Edison">Southern California Edison</a> (SCE) to examine the future of <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> in terms of how home and vehicle energy systems will work with the electrical grid. Under the multi-million-dollar, multi-year project, Ford will convert a demonstration fleet of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Hybrids</a> into plug-in hybrids, and SCE will evaluate how the vehicles might interact with the home and the utility's electrical grid. Some of the vehicles will be evaluated "in typical customer settings", according to Ford.<sup id="cite_ref-akhrum_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akhrum-16"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-edison_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edison-17"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>On June 12, 2008 <a href="/wiki/USDOE" title="USDOE" class="mw-redirect">USDOE</a> expanded its own fleet of alternative fuel and advanced technology vehicles with the addition of a Ford Escape Plug-In Hybrid Flex-Fuel Vehicle. The vehicle is equipped with a 10-kilowatt (13&#160;hp) <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion" title="Lithium-ion" class="mw-redirect">lithium-ion</a> battery supplied by <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Controls-Saft" title="Johnson Controls-Saft" class="mw-redirect">Johnson Controls-Saft</a> that stores enough electric energy to drive up to 30 miles (48&#160;km) at speeds of up to 40&#160;mph (64&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In March 2009 Ford launched to the U.S. market the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Ford Fusion Hybrid</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Milan_Hybrid" title="Mercury Milan Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Mercury Milan Hybrid</a>, both as 2010 models.<sup id="cite_ref-GreenCar0409_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenCar0409-71"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Ford is going to introduce a <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a> to challenge the <a href="/wiki/Chevy_Volt" title="Chevy Volt" class="mw-redirect">Chevy Volt</a> by 2012<sup id="cite_ref-autoblog_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autoblog-63"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-energy1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-energy1-72"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> and more <a href="/wiki/Charge-maintaining_hybrid" title="Charge-maintaining hybrid" class="mw-redirect">charge-maintaining hybrids</a> (traditional gas-electric hybrids), beginning with one in 2011.</p>

<p>Current and planned Ford hybrid electric vehicles:</p>

<ul>

<li>2004– <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Hybrid</a></li>

<li>2006– <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Mariner" title="Mercury Mariner">Mercury Mariner</a></li>

<li>2009– <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_Hybrid" title="Ford Fusion Hybrid">Ford Fusion Hybrid</a>/<a href="/wiki/Mercury_Milan" title="Mercury Milan">Mercury Milan</a></li>

<li>2009/10– <a href="/wiki/Ford_Edge" title="Ford Edge">Ford Edge</a>/<a href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKX" title="Lincoln MKX">Lincoln MKX</a></li>

</ul>

<h4> <span class="mw-headline" id="All-electric_vehicles">All-electric vehicles</span></h4>

<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/All-electric_vehicle" title="All-electric vehicle" class="mw-redirect">All-electric vehicle</a></div>

<p>Ford ended the <a href="/wiki/Think_City" title="Think City" class="mw-redirect">Think City</a> experiment and ordered all the cars repossessed and destroyed, even as many of the people leasing them begged to be able to buy the cars from Ford. After outcry from the lessees and activists in the US and Norway, Ford returned the cars to Norway for sale.</p>

<p>Bill Ford was one of the first top industry executives to make regular use of an <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">battery electric vehicle</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ranger_EV" title="Ford Ranger EV">Ford Ranger EV</a>, while the company contracted with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a> to deliver electric postal vans based on the Ranger EV platform..Ford discontinued a line of electric <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ranger" title="Ford Ranger">Ranger</a> <a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">pickup trucks</a> and ordered them destroyed, though it reversed in January 2005, after environmentalist protest.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>The North American <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(North_America)" title="Ford Focus (North America)" class="mw-redirect">Focus</a> EV is based on next generation Focus fuel vehicle, converted to an electric propulsion system as a Production EV by Magna International, and is planned to be launched in late 2011. Ford plans to have 10,000 Focus EVs on the road beginning in late 2011 in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Magna_International" title="Magna International">Magna International</a> and it will be a global vehicle that will be sold in the three key markets of North America, Europe and Asia-Pacific. The Focus EV has a maximum range of about 160 kilometers or 100 miles, and a top speed of about 120+ kilometers or 75+ miles per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Current and planned Ford electric vehicles:<sup id="cite_ref-autoblog_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autoblog-63"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-energy1_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-energy1-72"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<ul>

<li>2010 All-electric <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Connect" title="Ford Transit Connect">Transit Connect</a></li>

<li>2011 All-electric small car in late 2011 (<a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_EV" title="Ford Focus EV" class="mw-redirect">Ford Focus EV</a>).</li>

<li>2013 <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max" title="Ford C-Max">C-MAX Energi</a> coming fall 2012</li>

</ul>

<p>Ford <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">battery electric vehicle</a> (BEV) demonstrators are included in a British project that is part of the UK government's zero carbon vehicle fleet of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_BEV" title="Ford Focus BEV" class="mw-redirect">Focus BEVs</a>. The BEV demonstrator fleet is being developed partly with public funding from the government's <a href="/wiki/Technology_Strategy_Board" title="Technology Strategy Board">Technology Strategy Board</a> (TSB), which promotes innovative industry-led projects that reduce CO2 while benefiting the UK's transport system.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrogen">Hydrogen</span></h3>

<p>Ford also continues to study <a href="/wiki/Fuel_Cell" title="Fuel Cell" class="mw-redirect">Fuel Cell</a>-powered electric powertrains, and has demonstrated hydrogen-fueled <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> technologies, as well as developing the next-generation hybrid-electric systems. Compared with conventional vehicles, <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid vehicles</a> and/or <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cell</a> vehicles decrease air pollution emissions as well as sound levels, with favorable impacts upon respiratory health and decrease of <a href="/wiki/Noise_health_effects" title="Noise health effects" class="mw-redirect">noise health effects</a>.</p>

<p>Ford has launched the production of <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_vehicle" title="Hydrogen vehicle">hydrogen-powered</a> shuttle buses, using hydrogen instead of gasoline in a standard <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_vehicle#Hydrogen_internal_combustion" title="Hydrogen vehicle">internal combustion engine</a>, for use at airports and convention centers.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> At the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Auto_Show" title="Greater Los Angeles Auto Show" class="mw-redirect">Greater Los Angeles Auto Show</a>, Ford showcased a hydrogen fuel cell version of its Explorer SUV. The Fuel cell Explorer has a combined output of 174&#160;hp (130&#160;kW). It has a large hydrogen storage tank which is situated in the center of the car taking the original place of the conventional model's automatic transmission. The centered position of the tank assists the vehicle reach a notable range of 350 miles (563&#160;km), the farthest for a fuel cell vehicle so far. The fuel cell Explorer the first in a series of prototypes partly funded by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">United States Department of Energy</a> to expand efforts to determine the feasibility of hydrogen- powered vehicles. The fuel cell Explorer is one of several vehicles with green technology being featured at the L.A. show, including the 2008 Ford Escape Hybrid, PZEV emissions compliant Fusion and Focus models and a 2008 Ford F-Series Super Duty outfitted with Ford's clean diesel technology.</p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Increased_fuel_efficiency">Increased fuel efficiency</span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_EcoBoost_logo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/Ford_EcoBoost_logo.jpg/200px-Ford_EcoBoost_logo.jpg" width="200" height="117" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_EcoBoost_logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

All Ford's models with <a href="/wiki/EcoBoost" title="EcoBoost" class="mw-redirect">EcoBoost</a> engines are identified by Ford's leaf road logo badge.</div>

</div>

</div>

<p>Ford Motor Company announced it will accelerate its plans to produce more fuel-efficient cars, changing both its North American manufacturing plans and its lineup of vehicles available in the United States. In terms of North American manufacturing, the company will convert three existing truck and sport utility vehicle (SUV) plants for small car production, with the first conversion starting in December at its Michigan Truck Plant. In addition, Ford's assembly plants near Mexico City, Mexico, and in Louisville, Kentucky, will convert from pickups and SUVs to small cars, including the Ford Fiesta, by 2011. Ford will also introduce to North America six of its European small vehicles, including two versions of the Ford Fiesta, by the end of 2012. And last but not least, Ford is stepping up its production of fuel-efficient "<a href="/wiki/EcoBoost" title="EcoBoost" class="mw-redirect">EcoBoost</a>" V-6 and four-cylinder engines, while increasing its production of hybrid vehicles. See the Ford press release.</p>

<p>Ford of Europe developed the <a href="/wiki/ECOnetic" title="ECOnetic">ECOnetic</a> programme to address the market and legislative need for higher fuel efficiency and lower CO2 emissions. As opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_engine" title="Hybrid engine" class="mw-redirect">hybrid engine</a> technology used in competitor products such as the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">Toyota Prius</a>, ECOnetic improves existing technology. Using lower consuming <a href="/wiki/Ford_Duratorq_engine" title="Ford Duratorq engine">Duratorq TDCi</a> diesel engines, and based on a combination of improved aerodynamics, lower resistance and improved efficiency, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Ford Fiesta</a> is currently the lowest emitting mass-produced car in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" title="Ford Focus (international)" class="mw-redirect">2012 Ford Focus ECOnetic</a> will have better fuel consumption that the Prius or the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">Volkswagen Golf</a> <a href="/wiki/BlueMotion" title="BlueMotion">BlueMotion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> ECOnetic is not presently planned to be sold in North Americam due to current perceived lower consumer demand.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Ford has challenged University teams to create a vehicle that is simple, durable, lightweight and come equipped with a base target price of only $7,000 The students from <a href="/wiki/Aachen_University" title="Aachen University" class="mw-redirect">Aachen University</a> created the "<a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Ford_Model_T&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2015 Ford Model T (page does not exist)">2015 Ford Model T</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In 2000, under the leadership of the current Ford chairman, William Clay Ford, the Company announced<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> a planned 25 percent improvement in the average mileage of its light truck fleet – including its popular <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUVs</a> – to be completed by the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Calendar_year" title="Calendar year">calendar year</a>. In 2003, Ford announced that competitive market conditions and technological and cost challenges would prevent the company from achieving this goal.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>Researchers at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Massachusetts" title="University of Massachusetts">University of Massachusetts</a> have, however, listed Ford as the seventh-worst corporate producer of air pollution, primarily because of the <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a> compounds, <a href="/wiki/1,2,4-trimethylbenzene" title="1,2,4-trimethylbenzene" class="mw-redirect">1,2,4-trimethylbenzene</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Glycol_ethers" title="Glycol ethers">glycol ethers</a> released from its <a href="/wiki/Casting_(metalworking)" title="Casting (metalworking)">casting</a>, truck, and assembly plants.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The United States Environmental Protection Agency has linked Ford to 54 <a href="/wiki/Superfund" title="Superfund">Superfund</a> toxic waste sites, twelve of which have been cleaned up and deleted from the list.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>For the 2007 model year, Ford had thirteen U.S. models that achieve 30 miles per gallon or better (based on the highway fuel economy estimates of the EPA and several of Ford's vehicles were recognized in the EPA and Department of Energy Fuel Economy Guide for best-in-class fuel economy. Ford claimed to have eliminated nearly three million pounds of smog-forming emissions from their U.S. cars and light trucks over the 2004 to 2006 model years.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="PC_Power_Management">PC Power Management</span></h3>

<p>On March 2010, Ford announced its <a href="/wiki/PC_Power_Management" title="PC Power Management" class="mw-redirect">PC Power Management</a> system which it developed with NightWatchman software from <a href="/wiki/1E" title="1E">1E</a>. The company is expected to save $1.2m on power cost and reduce carbon footprint by an estimated 16,000 to 25,000 metric tons annually when the system is fully implemented.</p>

<p>PC power management is being rolled out to all Ford computer users in US this month and it will be used in Ford operations around the world later in the year. Computers with this power profile enabled will monitor its usage patterns and decides when it can be turned off. PC user will be alerted of the approaching power down time and given the opportunity to delay it.</p>

<p>According to company reduction in carbon footprint and power cost will be achieved by developing 'Power Profiles' for every PC in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Auto_racing">Auto racing</span></h2>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Stock_car_racing">Stock car racing</span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Todd_Kluever.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/Todd_Kluever.jpg/200px-Todd_Kluever.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Todd_Kluever.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

NASCAR <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_(Americas)" title="Ford Fusion (Americas)">Ford Fusion</a> race car</div>

</div>

</div>

<p>Ford is one of four manufacturers in <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>'s three major series: <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series" title="Sprint Cup Series">Sprint Cup Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nationwide_Series" title="Nationwide Series">Nationwide Series</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Camping_World_Truck_Series" title="Camping World Truck Series">Camping World Truck Series</a>. Major teams include <a href="/wiki/Roush_Fenway_Racing" title="Roush Fenway Racing">Roush Fenway Racing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yates_Racing" title="Yates Racing">Yates Racing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Petty_Motorsports." title="Richard Petty Motorsports." class="mw-redirect">Richard Petty Motorsports.</a> Ford is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Mid-size" title="Mid-size" class="mw-redirect">mid-size</a> <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_(North_American)" title="Ford Fusion (North American)" class="mw-redirect">Fusion</a> in the Sprint Cup, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Mustang</a> in the Nationwide Series, and by the <a href="/wiki/F-150" title="F-150" class="mw-redirect">F-150</a> in the Camping World Truck Series. Some of the most successful NASCAR Fords were the aerodynamic fastback <a href="/wiki/Ford_Torino" title="Ford Torino">Ford Torino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Torino_Talladega" title="Ford Torino Talladega">Ford Torino Talladega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Cyclone_Spoiler_II" title="Mercury Cyclone Spoiler II">Mercury Cyclone Spoiler II</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Montego" title="Mercury Montego">Mercury Montegos</a>, and the aero-era <a href="/wiki/Ford_Thunderbird" title="Ford Thunderbird">Ford Thunderbirds</a>. The Ford nameplate has won eight <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series#Manufacturer.27s_Championship" title="Sprint Cup Series">manufacturer's championships</a> in Sprint Cup, while Mercury has won one. The Ford Fusion is also used in the <a href="/wiki/ARCA_Remax_Series" title="ARCA Remax Series" class="mw-redirect">ARCA Remax Series</a>.</p>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benny_Parsons%27_1969_Ford_Talladega_Race_Car.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Benny_Parsons%27_1969_Ford_Talladega_Race_Car.jpg/220px-Benny_Parsons%27_1969_Ford_Talladega_Race_Car.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benny_Parsons%27_1969_Ford_Talladega_Race_Car.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

Benny Parsons' 1969 Ford Torino Talladega ARCA Championship Race Car owned by Barry Miller of Portland Indiana</div>

</div>

</div>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Formula_One">Formula One</span></h3>

<div class="thumb tleft">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stewart_gp_barrichello_1998.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Stewart_gp_barrichello_1998.jpg/160px-Stewart_gp_barrichello_1998.jpg" width="160" height="106" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stewart_gp_barrichello_1998.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

<a href="/wiki/Rubens_Barrichello" title="Rubens Barrichello">Rubens Barrichello</a> driving for the <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Grand_Prix" title="Stewart Grand Prix">Stewart Grand Prix</a> team in 1997</div>

</div>

</div>

<p>Ford was heavily involved in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> for many years, and supplied engines to a large number of teams from 1967 until 2004. These engines were designed and manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Cosworth" title="Cosworth">Cosworth</a>, the racing division that was owned by Ford from 1998 to 2004. Ford-badged engines won 176 Grands Prix between 1967 and 2003 for teams such as <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus" title="Team Lotus">Team Lotus</a> and <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a>. Ford entered Formula One as a constructor in 2000 under the <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Racing" title="Jaguar Racing">Jaguar Racing</a> name, after buying the <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Grand_Prix" title="Stewart Grand Prix">Stewart Grand Prix</a> team which had been its primary 'works' team in the series since 1997. Jaguar achieved little success in Formula One, and after a turbulent five seasons, Ford withdrew from the category after the <a href="/wiki/2004_Formula_One_season" title="2004 Formula One season">2004 season</a>, selling both Jaguar Racing (which became <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull Racing</a>) and Cosworth (to <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Forsythe" title="Gerald Forsythe">Gerald Forsythe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Kalkhoven" title="Kevin Kalkhoven">Kevin Kalkhoven</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Rally">Rally</span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg/200px-Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Neste_Oil_Rally_2010_-_Jari-Matti_Latvala_in_shakedown.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

<a href="/wiki/Jari-Matti_Latvala" title="Jari-Matti Latvala">Jari-Matti Latvala</a> driving the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_RS_WRC_09" title="Ford Focus RS WRC 09" class="mw-redirect">Ford Focus RS WRC 09</a> in 2010.</div>

</div>

</div>

<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_World_Rally_Team" title="Ford World Rally Team">Ford World Rally Team</a></div>

<p>Ford has a long history in <a href="/wiki/Rallying" title="Rallying">rallying</a> and has been active in the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">World Rally Championship</a> since the beginning of the world championship, the <a href="/wiki/1973_World_Rally_Championship_season" title="1973 World Rally Championship season">1973 season</a>. Ford took the <a href="/wiki/1979_World_Rally_Championship_season" title="1979 World Rally Championship season">1979</a> manufacturers' title with <a href="/wiki/Hannu_Mikkola" title="Hannu Mikkola">Hannu Mikkola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Waldeg%C3%A5rd" title="Björn Waldegård">Björn Waldegård</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ari_Vatanen" title="Ari Vatanen">Ari Vatanen</a> driving the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_RS1800" title="Ford Escort RS1800" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escort RS1800</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Group_B" title="Group B">Group B</a> era, Ford achieved success with <a href="/wiki/Ford_RS200" title="Ford RS200">Ford RS200</a>. Since the <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Rally_Championship_season" title="1999 World Rally Championship season">1999 season</a>, Ford has used various versions of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_WRC" title="Ford Focus WRC" class="mw-redirect">Ford Focus WRC</a> to much success. In the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Rally_Championship_season" title="2006 World Rally Championship season">2006 season</a>, <a href="/wiki/BP-Ford_World_Rally_Team" title="BP-Ford World Rally Team" class="mw-redirect">BP-Ford World Rally Team</a> secured Ford its second manufacturers' title, with the Focus RS WRC 06 built by <a href="/wiki/M-Sport" title="M-Sport">M-Sport</a> and driven by <i><a href="/wiki/Flying_Finn_(sports)" title="Flying Finn (sports)" class="mw-redirect">Flying Finns</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Gr%C3%B6nholm" title="Marcus Grönholm">Marcus Grönholm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mikko_Hirvonen" title="Mikko Hirvonen">Mikko Hirvonen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Continuing with Grönholm and Hirvonen, Ford successfully defended the manufacturers' world championship in the <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Rally_Championship_season" title="2007 World Rally Championship season">2007 season</a>. Ford is the only manufacturer to score in the points for 92 consecutive races; since the <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Rally_Championship_season" title="2002 World Rally Championship season">2002 season</a> opener <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo_Rally" title="Monte Carlo Rally">Monte Carlo Rally</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_cars">Sports cars</span></h3>

<div class="thumb tleft">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GT40_at_Goodwood.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/GT40_at_Goodwood.jpg/220px-GT40_at_Goodwood.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GT40_at_Goodwood.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

<a href="/wiki/Ford_GT40" title="Ford GT40">Ford GT40</a></div>

</div>

</div>

<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_GT#Racing" title="Ford GT">Ford GT#Racing</a></div>

<p>Ford sports cars have been visible in the world of sports car racing since 1964. Most notably the <a href="/wiki/GT40" title="GT40">GT40</a> won the <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a> four times in the 1960s and is the only American car to ever win overall at this prestigious event. Ford also won the <a href="/wiki/1968_International_Championship_for_Makes" title="1968 International Championship for Makes" class="mw-redirect">1968 International Championship for Makes</a> with the GT40, which still stands today as one of the all-time greatest racing cars. Swiss team <a href="/wiki/Matech_GT_Racing" title="Matech GT Racing" class="mw-redirect">Matech GT Racing</a>, in collaboration with Ford Racing, opened a new chapter with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_GT" title="Ford GT">Ford GT</a>, winning the Teams title in the 2008 <a href="/wiki/FIA_GT3_European_Championship" title="FIA GT3 European Championship">FIA GT3 European Championship</a>.</p>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbers02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Barbers02.jpg/220px-Barbers02.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbers02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

<a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang GT</a> (racing GT car)</div>

</div>

</div>

<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang#Racing" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang#Racing</a></div>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang</a> has arguably been Ford's most successful sports car. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jerry_Titus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jerry Titus (page does not exist)">Jerry Titus</a> won the 1965 SCCA Pro B National Championship with a Mustang and the model went on to earn Ford the SCCA <a href="/wiki/Trans-Am_Championship" title="Trans-Am Championship" class="mw-redirect">Trans-Am Championship</a> title in both 1966 and 1967. Ford won the Trans-Am Championship again in 1970 with <a href="/wiki/Parnelli_Jones" title="Parnelli Jones">Parnelli Jones</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Folmer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="George Folmer (page does not exist)">George Folmer</a> driving <a href="/wiki/Boss_302_Mustang" title="Boss 302 Mustang">Boss 302 Mustangs</a> for <a href="/wiki/Bud_Moore_Engineering" title="Bud Moore Engineering">Bud Moore Engineering</a>. Ford took the 1985 and 1986 IMSA GTO Championship with Mustangs driven by <a href="/wiki/John_Jones_(driver)" title="John Jones (driver)" class="mw-redirect">John Jones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Pruett" title="Scott Pruett">Scott Pruett</a> before returning to Trans-Am glory with a championship in 1989 with <a href="/wiki/Dorsey_Schroeder" title="Dorsey Schroeder">Dorsey Schroeder</a>. Ford dominated Trans-Am in the 1990s with <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tommy_Kendal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tommy Kendal (page does not exist)">Tommy Kendal</a> winning championships in 1993, 1995, 1996, and 1997 with <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Gentilozi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Paul Gentilozi (page does not exist)">Paul Gentilozi</a> adding yet another title in 1999. In 2005 the Ford Mustang FR500C took the championship in the Rolex <a href="/wiki/Koni_Challenge" title="Koni Challenge" class="mw-redirect">Koni Challenge</a> Series in its first year on the circuit. In 2007 Ford added a victory in the GT4 European Championship. 2008 was the first year of the Mustang Challenge for the Miller Cup, a series which pits a full field of identical factory built Ford Mustang race cars against each other. Also in 2008, Ford won the manufacturers championship in the Koni Challenge Series and HyperSport drivers Joe Foster and Steve Maxwell won the drivers title in a Mustang GT.</p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Touring_cars">Touring cars</span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Winterbottom2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Winterbottom2008.jpg/220px-Winterbottom2008.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Winterbottom2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

<a href="/wiki/Ford_Performance_Racing" title="Ford Performance Racing">Ford Performance Racing</a> <a href="/wiki/Ford_Falcon_(Australia)" title="Ford Falcon (Australia)">Ford Falcon</a> <a href="/wiki/V8_Supercar" title="V8 Supercar" class="mw-redirect">V8 Supercar</a> at Eastern Creek in Australia in 2008.</div>

</div>

</div>

<p>Ford has campaigned touring cars such as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" title="Ford Focus (international)" class="mw-redirect">Focus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Falcon_(Australia)" title="Ford Falcon (Australia)">Falcon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Contour" title="Ford Contour">Contour</a>/<a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Mondeo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Sierra</a> <a href="/wiki/Cosworth" title="Cosworth">Cosworth</a> in many different series throughout the years. Notably, Mondeo drivers finished 1,2,3 in the 2000 <a href="/wiki/British_Touring_Car_Championship" title="British Touring Car Championship">British Touring Car Championship</a> and Falcon drivers placed 1,2,3 in the <a href="/wiki/2005_V8_Supercar_Championship_Series" title="2005 V8 Supercar Championship Series">2005 V8 Supercar Championship Series</a>.</p>

<h3> <span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span></h3>

<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_500" title="Indianapolis 500">Indianapolis 500</a>, Ford powered <a href="/wiki/American_Championship_Car_Racing" title="American Championship Car Racing" class="mw-redirect">IndyCars</a> won 17 times between 1965 and 1996<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources from November 2010">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Ford has also branched out into drifting with the introduction of the new model Mustang. Most noticeable is the Turquoise and Blue Falken Tires Mustang driven by Vaughn Gittin Jr, A.K.A. "JR". with 750 RWHP (Rear Wheel Horsepower). In <a href="/wiki/Drag_racing" title="Drag racing">drag racing</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Force_Racing" title="John Force Racing">John Force Racing</a> drivers <a href="/wiki/John_Force" title="John Force">John Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Pedregon" title="Tony Pedregon">Tony Pedregon</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Hight&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Robert Hight (page does not exist)">Robert Hight</a> have piloted <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang</a> <a href="/wiki/Funny_Car" title="Funny Car">Funny Cars</a> to several <a href="/wiki/National_Hot_Rod_Association" title="National Hot Rod Association">NHRA</a> titles in recent seasons. Teammates <a href="/wiki/Tim_Wilkerson" title="Tim Wilkerson">Tim Wilkerson</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bob_Tasca_III&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bob Tasca III (page does not exist)">Bob Tasca III</a> also drive Mustangs in Funny Car. <a href="/wiki/Formula_Ford" title="Formula Ford">Formula Ford</a>, a formula for single-seater cars without wings and originally on road tires were conceived in 1966 in the UK as an entry-level formula for racing drivers. Many of today's racing drivers started their car racing careers in this category.</p>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Ford_trucks">Ford trucks</span></h2>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_1961.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/84/Ford_1961.JPG/200px-Ford_1961.JPG" width="200" height="252" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_1961.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

1961 Ford H-Series trucks</div>

</div>

</div>

<div class="thumb tleft">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_1939.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b5/Ford_1939.jpg/200px-Ford_1939.jpg" width="200" height="131" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_1939.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

1939 Ford pick-up truck</div>

</div>

</div>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GAZ-AA_in_Technical_museum_Togliatti.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/GAZ-AA_in_Technical_museum_Togliatti.JPG/200px-GAZ-AA_in_Technical_museum_Togliatti.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GAZ-AA_in_Technical_museum_Togliatti.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

A Ford truck like those used by both armies to resupply their troops in the <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">Chaco War</a>.</div>

</div>

</div>

<p>Ford has produced trucks since 1908. Countries where Ford commercial vehicles are or were made include Argentina, Australia, Brazil, Canada (badged <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(automobile)" title="Mercury (automobile)">Mercury</a> too), France, Germany, India, Netherlands, Philippines, Spain (badged <a href="/wiki/Ebro_trucks" title="Ebro trucks">Ebro</a> too), Turkey, UK (badged also <a href="/wiki/Fordson" title="Fordson" class="mw-redirect">Fordson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thames_Trader" title="Thames Trader">Thames</a>) and USA.</p>

<p>From the 1940s to late 1970s Ford's <a href="/wiki/Ford_F-Series" title="Ford F-Series">Ford F-Series</a> were used as the base for light trucks for the North American market.</p>

<p>Most of these ventures are now extinct. The European one that lasted longest was the lorries arm of <a href="/wiki/Ford_of_Britain" title="Ford of Britain">Ford of Britain</a>, which was eventually sold to <a href="/wiki/Iveco" title="Iveco">Iveco</a> group in 1986, and whose last significant models were the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transcontinental" title="Ford Transcontinental">Transcontinental</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cargo_(Europe)" title="Ford Cargo (Europe)" class="mw-redirect">Cargo</a>.</p>

<p>In the United States, Ford's heavy trucks division (<a href="/wiki/Truck_classification" title="Truck classification">Classes 7 and 8</a>) was sold in 1997 to <a href="/wiki/Freightliner_Trucks" title="Freightliner Trucks">Freightliner Trucks</a>, which rebranded the lineup as <a href="/wiki/Sterling_Trucks" title="Sterling Trucks">Sterling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sterling_news_release_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sterling_news_release-92"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Freightliner is in the process of discontinuing this line.</p>

<p>Line of heavy trucks made by Ford for the North American market:</p>

<ul>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_F-650" title="Ford F-650">Ford F-650</a> – joint venture model from 2000 to present</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_L-Series_Trucks" title="Ford L-Series Trucks">Ford L9000</a> – last model year 1999</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_L-Series_Trucks" title="Ford L-Series Trucks">Ford LNT9000</a> – short nose tandem axle from 1970s to 1997</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_L-Series_Trucks" title="Ford L-Series Trucks">Ford LT9000</a> – tandem axle with last model year 1997</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_L-Series_Trucks" title="Ford L-Series Trucks">Ford FT900</a> – until 1998</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_L-Series_Trucks" title="Ford L-Series Trucks">Ford LT8000</a> – last model year 1998</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_L-Series_Trucks" title="Ford L-Series Trucks">Ford L7000</a> – last model year 1996</li>

</ul>

<p>Ford continues to manufacture medium duty trucks under the <a href="/wiki/F-650" title="F-650" class="mw-redirect">F-650</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_F-650" title="Ford F-650">F-750</a> badges. In 2001, the company entered into a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Navistar_International" title="Navistar International">Navistar International</a> to produce medium duty commercial trucks.<sup id="cite_ref-BD1_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BD1-93"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> The first new model from the new corporation, known as Blue Diamond Truck Company LLC,<sup id="cite_ref-BD1_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BD1-93"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> was the 2006 model year LCF,<sup id="cite_ref-LCF1_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LCF1-94"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> the first Ford branded cab-over-engine design in the United States since Freightliner's acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cargo" title="Ford Cargo">Cargo</a> in the mid-1990s.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources from February 2011">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The LCF was discontinued in 2009<sup id="cite_ref-LCF2_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LCF2-95"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> and Ford's 2011 medium-duty commercial offerings are limited to the two F-Series.<sup id="cite_ref-Med1_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Med1-96"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In 1999 the end of the F800 meant Ford was not producing in any F-series heavy truck chassis.</p>

<p>In Europe, Ford manufactures the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit" title="Ford Transit">Ford Transit</a> jumbo van which is classed as a Large Goods Vehicle and has a payload of up to 2,265&#160;kg, there are options of a panel van, pickup or chassis cab. The Ford Transit is also available as a light van called the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Connect" title="Ford Transit Connect">Ford Transit Connect</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ranger" title="Ford Ranger">Ford Ranger</a> pickup is available.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_products">Bus products</span></h2>

<p>Ford manufactured complete buses in the company's early history, but today the role of the company has changed to that of a <a href="/wiki/Second_stage_manufacturer" title="Second stage manufacturer">second stage manufacturer</a>. In North America, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_E-Series" title="Ford E-Series">E-Series</a> is still used as a chassis for small school buses and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_F-650" title="Ford F-650">F-650</a> is used in commercial bus markets. In the 1980s and 1990s, the medium-duty <a href="/wiki/Ford_B-Series" title="Ford B-Series">B700</a> was a popular chassis used by school bus body manufacturers (<a href="/wiki/Thomas_Built_Buses" title="Thomas Built Buses">Thomas Built</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ward_Body_Works" title="Ward Body Works">Ward</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_Bird_Corporation" title="Blue Bird Corporation">Blue Bird</a>, etc...), but Ford lost its market share due to industry contraction and agreements between body manufacturers. Older bus models included:</p>

<p>Prior to 1939, For buses were based on truck bodies:</p>

<ul>

<li>Model B – 1930s</li>

<li>Model T – 1920s</li>

<li>F-105 school bus</li>

</ul>

<p>During World War II Ford manufactured <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_bus" title="Ford Transit bus">Ford Transit bus</a>, a series of small transit buses with bodies built by second party<sup id="cite_ref-detroittransithistory.info_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-detroittransithistory.info-98"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup>:</p>

<ul>

<li>09-B/19-B City transit bus – 1939–1941</li>

<li>19-B/29-B City transit bus – 1941–1942</li>

<li>49-B/79-B City transit bus – 1944–1947</li>

<li>69-B City transit bus – 1946–1947</li>

<li>29-B City transit bus – 1946–1947</li>

<li>72-T transit bus – 1944–1945</li>

</ul>

<p>After 1946 the Transit City bus was sold as <i>Universal Bus</i> with the roof changed from fabric/wood to all metal:</p>

<ul>

<li>79-B Universal transit bus – 1946–1947</li>

</ul>

<p>Succeeding the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_bus" title="Ford Transit bus">Ford Transit bus</a> was the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ford_8M&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ford 8M (page does not exist)">Ford 8M</a> buses:</p>

<ul>

<li>8MB transit bus – with Wayne Works 1948–?</li>

</ul>

<p>Following World War II and from 1950s onwards Ford lost out to <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-detroittransithistory.info_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-detroittransithistory.info-98"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> This led to the end of transit buses for Ford in North America.</p>

<ul>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_B-Series" title="Ford B-Series">B500 or B-series</a> – 1950-1990s based on Ford F-series truck chassis used by school bus body manufacturers</li>

</ul>

<p>In Europe, Ford manufactures the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit" title="Ford Transit">Ford Transit</a> <a href="/wiki/Minibus" title="Minibus">Minibus</a> which is classed in Europe as a Passenger Carrying Vehicle and there are options of 12, 15 or 17 seaters.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> In the past European models included:</p>

<ul>

<li>EM</li>

<li>N-138</li>

<li>D series buses (Australia)</li>

</ul>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Ford_tractors">Ford tractors</span></h2>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford-Tractor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Ford-Tractor.jpg/200px-Ford-Tractor.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford-Tractor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

Ford tractor</div>

</div>

</div>

<p>The "Henry Ford and Son Company" began making <a href="/wiki/Fordson_tractor" title="Fordson tractor">Fordson tractors</a> in Henry's hometown of Springwells (later part of <a href="/wiki/Dearborn,_Michigan" title="Dearborn, Michigan">Dearborn</a>, Michigan from 1907 to 1928, from 1919 to 1932, at <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>, Ireland and 1933–1964 at <a href="/wiki/Ford_Dagenham" title="Ford Dagenham">Dagenham</a>, England, later transferred to <a href="/wiki/Basildon" title="Basildon">Basildon</a>. They were also produced in <a href="/wiki/Leningrad" title="Leningrad" class="mw-redirect">Leningrad</a> beginning in 1924.</p>

<p>In 1986, Ford expanded its tractor business when it purchased the Sperry-New Holland skid-steer loader and hay baler, hay tools and implement company from <a href="/wiki/Sperry_Corporation" title="Sperry Corporation">Sperry Corporation</a> and formed Ford-New Holland which bought out <a href="/wiki/Versatile" title="Versatile">Versatile</a> tractors in 1988. This company was bought by <a href="/wiki/Fiat" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> in 1993 and the name changed from Ford New Holland to New Holland. <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_Ag" title="New Holland Ag" class="mw-redirect">New Holland</a> is now part of <a href="/wiki/CNH_Global" title="CNH Global" class="mw-redirect">CNH Global</a>.</p>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_ford_1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Henry_ford_1919.jpg/100px-Henry_ford_1919.jpg" width="100" height="128" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_ford_1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

<a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a> (ca. 1919)</div>

</div>

</div>

<div class="thumb tleft">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1896-ford-archives.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/1896-ford-archives.jpg/200px-1896-ford-archives.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1896-ford-archives.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/skins-1.18/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>

1896 Ford Quadricycle</div>

</div>

</div>

<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ford_Motor_Company" title="History of Ford Motor Company">History of Ford Motor Company</a></div>

<p>The Ford Motor Company was launched in a converted factory in 1903 with $28,000 in cash from twelve investors, most notably <a href="/wiki/John_Francis_Dodge" title="John Francis Dodge">John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horace_Elgin_Dodge" title="Horace Elgin Dodge">Horace Dodge</a> (who would later found <a href="/wiki/Dodge_Brothers_Motor_Vehicle_Company" title="Dodge Brothers Motor Vehicle Company" class="mw-redirect">their own</a> car company). Later Ford realized it would be better if he manufactured all of his company's automotive parts himself instead of using parts from aftermarket sources which lead to the production of the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly line</a> 1908. Henry's first attempt under his name was the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford_Company" title="Henry Ford Company">Henry Ford Company</a> on November 3, 1901, which became the <a href="/wiki/Cadillac_Motor_Company" title="Cadillac Motor Company" class="mw-redirect">Cadillac Motor Company</a> on August 22, 1902. In 1908 Ford During its early years, the company produced just a few cars a day at its factory on Mack Avenue in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>. Groups of two or three men worked on each car from components made to order by other companies. Henry Ford was 40 years old when he founded the Ford Motor Company, which would go on to become one of the world's largest and most profitable companies, as well as being one to survive the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>. As one of the largest family-controlled companies in the world, the Ford Motor Company has been in continuous family control for over 100 years.</p>

"Fording the Atlantic: Ford and Fordism in Europe" in <i>Business History</i> Volume 47, #January 1, 2005 pp 122–127</li>
